  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

If she is ever to live free, Rachel must first walk willingly into the demonic ever-after in search of long-lost ancient knowledge.<br /><br />But when you dance with demons, you lay your soul on the line . . . and there are some lines that should never be crossed.</span>

<a href="/questions/1186828-i-m-flummoxed-when-the-frell-did">I&#39;m flummoxed...when the frell did Marshall appear in Cincinnati? Going by Rachel&#39;s comments, it seems there&#39;s a story there, but he seems to spawn between books 5 &amp;6. Please help!</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/38121301-jennifer-snider-byrd"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1419102017i/38121301._UY100_CR25,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/38121301-jennifer-snider-byrd">Jennifer Snider Byrd</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
Rachel met Marshall in Book 4 when she was helping Nick out of town. Marshall then shows up in Cincinnati in book 6 for a job interview. 
</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2311619150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11404860512252794416">This one was a treat to read. I have little going on about how to describe the reading experience, except for the fact that there was little romance in this book. That helped. There was also little action too.<br/><br/>So what did this book comprise? There are continuations about relationships. The mourning of lost ones. The fear of the unknown, here called the ever after, which is a dimension where demons live.<br/><br/>I thought hard about whether this book is worth 4 stars. But then I realized that though I will</span>
  <span id="freeText11404860512252794416" style="display:none">This one was a treat to read. I have little going on about how to describe the reading experience, except for the fact that there was little romance in this book. That helped. There was also little action too.<br /><br />So what did this book comprise? There are continuations about relationships. The mourning of lost ones. The fear of the unknown, here called the ever after, which is a dimension where demons live.<br /><br />I thought hard about whether this book is worth 4 stars. But then I realized that though I will never reread this book, it's a pretty damn well put together one. The last third is the good stuff. The author, Kim Harrison, is a master storyteller. You can't go wrong with her.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1177586228?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007578887" href="/book/show/22388321-where-demons-dare">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">urban fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1177586228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2489081134115849755">It's a fact that this book was not as good as the previous novel in the series but in no way is it no good, hence the 5 stars. The plot thickens more and we still have no clue as to who killed <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Kisten <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I will admit I may be a little bit bothered by that. But this book took a complete different turn.<br/><br/>Rachel is still struggling with her feelings and she is extra reckless, I'd say. She's grown so much as a person since book 1 and I'm proud of where she is but I'd lie</span>
  <span id="freeText2489081134115849755" style="display:none">It's a fact that this book was not as good as the previous novel in the series but in no way is it no good, hence the 5 stars. The plot thickens more and we still have no clue as to who killed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kisten <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I will admit I may be a little bit bothered by that. But this book took a complete different turn.<br /><br />Rachel is still struggling with her feelings and she is extra reckless, I'd say. She's grown so much as a person since book 1 and I'm proud of where she is but I'd lie if I'd say that thing don't get fucked up in this book for her and I thought it impossible for her situation to get any worse. <br /><br />If you've loved all the previous books, then there's no doubt that you'll like this one too for the simple reason that the author still manages to keep everything interesting. I haven't lost interest yet.<br /><br />If you wait for some Rachel-Ivy action then you may get disappointed.. I did, too. I'm not a hardcore shipper but there's an undeniable love between them and a bond too, that could easily evolve into something else if Rachel gave them a chance. At the end of the day, I just want them to be happy.<br /><br />I'll dive into the next book soon and hope we get some answers because I'm dying to see the person responsible for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kisten's <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> death suffer the same fate. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2489081134115849755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2289941138392457934" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/07/mini-reviews-for-a-few-demons-more-the-outlaw-demon-wails-by-kim-harrison.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>I mentioned in my review of <b>

    <i>For a Few Demons More</i>

</b> that Al was in trouble with the demons and wanted Rachel to help him out . . .<br><br>Yeah, guess how well that went over . . .<br><br>It didn't.<br><br>So Al's HELLA pissed (b/c he's a total blame shifter) and in demon jail, but only during the day, b/c he's arranged for someone to summon him to the real world as soon as the sun sets everyday.<br><br>But who? Hmmm?? Probably not who you're thinking . . .<br><br>Regardless of who is doing it, Al's getting out every night for the express purpose of terrorizing Rachel and her loved ones. He's a demon with nothing to lose, and a demon with nothing to lose is <i>not</i> a happy or fun demon.<br><br>So that's a problem.<br><br>But that's not all, b/c this is another installment with ALL THE THINGS happening, and it is as fantastic as <i>For a Few Demons More</i>.<br><br>We finally (finally, FINALLY) get some Ivy and Rachel resolution. FINALLY. Rachel finds out what really happened to her dad. Ceri has some BIG news, which prompts Trent to ask Rachel to go to the ever after with him (just like their fathers), and, oh yeah, Marshal (of scuba diving, Mackinaw fame) shows up on Rachel's doorstep, and so does a teenage gargoyle who likes to spit.&lt;------Bis is an awesome addition to the gang.<br><br>A few more really Big Deals happen, but that's all I can give you without spoilers. <div id="review_198949862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198949862" />
    <a title="jD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2415283-jd"><img alt="jD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283353615p2/2415283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198949862?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jD" href="/user/show/2415283-jd">jD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=library-yes">library-yes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=fantasy_urban">fantasy_urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198949862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1736373025085287696">In a nutshell, this was one of the best I have read so far. Why...<br/>Rachael -- more mature<br/>Ivy -- more sane<br/>Jenks -- still keeping it real<br/>Ceri -- big suprises<br/>Al -- big suprises<br/>Kristen -- still dead<br/>Rachael's Mom -- big suprises<br/>Trent -- whoa is me. I love him but he doesn't give me much to work with.<br/><br/>In this installment, Rachael has to face some rough truths. My heart went out to her as she struggled with so many variables. I didn't get frustrated with her decision-making process as in previous books b</span>
  <span id="freeText1736373025085287696" style="display:none">In a nutshell, this was one of the best I have read so far. Why...<br />Rachael -- more mature<br />Ivy -- more sane<br />Jenks -- still keeping it real<br />Ceri -- big suprises<br />Al -- big suprises<br />Kristen -- still dead<br />Rachael's Mom -- big suprises<br />Trent -- whoa is me. I love him but he doesn't give me much to work with.<br /><br />In this installment, Rachael has to face some rough truths. My heart went out to her as she struggled with so many variables. I didn't get frustrated with her decision-making process as in previous books because she actually took a minute to think. That was new and I embraced her as a woman who learned from her mistakes.<br /><br />Al is back and on a rampage. No one is safe from his constant attempts at vengence against Rachael. She has to deal with him and she does. Trent discovers there is dna in the Ever After that can help him restore fertility to the Elves. He hires Rachael to go with him as his protector. The journey doesn't take up many pages overall but what we learn changes things forever. <br /><br />Ms. Harrison put Rachael and her friends through some paces but I loved where it all ended. Although Rachael didn't hookup with Trent, I'm still hopeful but realize it would be a major plot development that won't happen overnight. There are plenty of demons in this book and we get to see more of the world they inhabit. Although Al is a sick puppy, I like the character and am glad he was such a big part of this story. A new character, Blis, has moved into Rachael's church. He is a gargoyle and we don't learn much about him in this book. I expect that will change going forward. Rachael has a new 'love' interest whose name I already forgot. He is boring but I am hopeful that shiny new penny is more than it appears. The biggest plot development for me was seeing the drama level go down a notch with Ivy. I actully understand her better and am hoping she continues to find a balance for herself and her friendship with Rachael. I am sure Ms. Harrison will make me eat those words at some point but I wanted to at least get it down in writing for the record. <br /><br />I am going to continue with the series as I am now addicted. I have 3 to go before I am caught up. Book 7 is not loved by the series fans so I expect to read that one slower. I have basically gobbled the others down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1736373025085287696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brighid " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brighid " href="/user/show/6193784-brighid">Brighid </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313214529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5077287129543353765">Let me first get the biggest rant out of the way first and foremost. I usually ingest all my books via audiobook format. There are some really good folks that do the reading and lots of so so folks. The first 4 books were read by Marguerite Gavin who did a bang up job with all the characters. As she is a great reader, all the characters had their distinct voice and mannerisms and she kept on target perfectly. Then all of the sudden she is replaced by Gigi Bermingham who screwed it up royally. Ob</span>
  <span id="freeText5077287129543353765" style="display:none">Let me first get the biggest rant out of the way first and foremost. I usually ingest all my books via audiobook format. There are some really good folks that do the reading and lots of so so folks. The first 4 books were read by Marguerite Gavin who did a bang up job with all the characters. As she is a great reader, all the characters had their distinct voice and mannerisms and she kept on target perfectly. Then all of the sudden she is replaced by Gigi Bermingham who screwed it up royally. Obviously there was a serious breakdown in the editing and publishing of this book. <br /> First the reader decided that lots of established characters and places should be pronounced totally differently than the previous 4 books. How aggravating! How could the publisher and editor let this through? Didn't this reader even listen to some of the previous audiobooks to get a clue? Didn't the management even listen to the audiotapes before publishing it?<br /> Next is the unfortunate issue that the reader did not have the talent to portray the different characters with different voice inflection. Well, she did try but she kept getting screwed up and switching them all up. How annoying! The worst voice was her grating portrayal of Jenks.<br /> This reader ruined the book for me. She is not truely to blame as any reader depends on her team and this team f*ed up. I do see that they go back to the original reader after this book so I will continue with the series. Phew!<br /> All in all I am enjoying this series. I do take exception to some truely stupid things that the main character Rachel Morgan does. I think she shows too much fear for a person in her line of work and she is way too much of a prude as well. Sometimes she has flashes of cleverness but then slaps herself with moments of stupid naievity that makes me scream in my head. Arrrrrggg!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5077287129543353765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/345066-schnaucl?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/345066-schnaucl?shelf=urban_fantasy">urban_fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/345066-schnaucl?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/345066-schnaucl?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/345066-schnaucl?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer16923026&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16923026" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10454067258716404677"><b>Warning: This review contains major spoilers for this book and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30259.For_a_Few_Demons_More__The_Hollows___5_' title='For a Few Demons More (The Hollows, #5) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'> For A Few Demons More</a></b><br/><br/>According to Kim Harrison, this was originally going to be the conclusion of the series and in some respects that really shows. Save for one or two things, the ending of the book could have been the sort of satisfying conclusion of the series. Kist's killer still hasn't been found, but considering that she didn't realize until she was writing book 7 that he needed to die in book 5 she did a remarkable job of wor</span>
  <span id="freeText10454067258716404677" style="display:none"><b>Warning: This review contains major spoilers for this book and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30259.For_a_Few_Demons_More__The_Hollows___5_" title="For a Few Demons More (The Hollows, #5) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener"> For A Few Demons More</a></b><br /><br />According to Kim Harrison, this was originally going to be the conclusion of the series and in some respects that really shows. Save for one or two things, the ending of the book could have been the sort of satisfying conclusion of the series. Kist's killer still hasn't been found, but considering that she didn't realize until she was writing book 7 that he needed to die in book 5 she did a remarkable job of working in everyone's grief. In fact, if I hadn't herd her say that she had to go back and work all that in I'd never have known that wasn't part of the plan. And Jenks mortality is still an issue, though frankly Matalina seems much closer to not surviving the winter. <br /><br />I think part of what makes it feel like a conclusion is that Rachel really has grown up. She's thinking before reacting more often now. She's not just saying she should grow up, she's doing it. And she's clearly starting a new phase in her life.<br /><br />I'm a little sad about where things ended up with Ivy. I suppose I should be happy that she clearly does like Ivy for Ivy and not just the vamp pheromones, something which Ivy finally knows, too. But my hope for anything but a close friendship has died. I can't argue that it doesn't make sense. Clearly it's safer for everyone this way and I've always been really turned off by the idea of a vampire literally owning and controlling another person, even if love is involved. Plus, I've never been a fan of selective bisexuality. Ivy is clearly bi and that's great, but the only woman Rachel's ever been sexually attracted to is Ivy and so on some level it's hard for me to believe it's anything more than vamp pheromones. We'll see. Right now my money's on Rachel ending up with Trent.<br /><br />As for the story itself, I enjoyed it. It was interesting to see the Ever After. I'd like it if the gargoyle became a reoccurring character. I am worried about Matlalina though. Even if Jenks can be saved I'm not sure he'd particularly want to be if she were gone. I'm ready to be done with Marshall. The white knight thing gets old very quickly where the woman in question is more than capable of taking care of herself better than the knight could even dream of doing. And it was fun seeing more of Rachel's mom. It goes a long way toward explaining why Rachel is the way she is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10454067258716404677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578797509?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" href="/user/show/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer">Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578797509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15366492278629016250">With everything that happened in book five, all the drama, tragedy and heartache, it was hard not being a little nervous about what Harrison would throw our way this time. But with a brave smile on my face, I dived right in. There was no way that I couldn't. I had to know what happened next. <br/><br/>I am so very glad that I waited to start this series until all the books were out because binge reading this series is so the way to go. They are so addicting and hard to put down and with so much on the lin</span>
  <span id="freeText15366492278629016250" style="display:none">With everything that happened in book five, all the drama, tragedy and heartache, it was hard not being a little nervous about what Harrison would throw our way this time. But with a brave smile on my face, I dived right in. There was no way that I couldn't. I had to know what happened next. <br /><br />I am so very glad that I waited to start this series until all the books were out because binge reading this series is so the way to go. They are so addicting and hard to put down and with so much on the line for Rachel, I couldn't see having to wait months for the next book, I think it would have killed me. <br /><br />Harrison has no qualms at all about putting her readers through the ringer. This woman does not pull her punches and with this novel focusing more on the gang and Rachel's personal life, things get real, and they get real, real fast. <br /><br />As much as this is Rachel's story, it is also Al's and Ceri's as well. We finally get background info on them both and even Trent as well and so much is starting to make sense and come together. It truly was mind blowing how many twists and unexpected turns showed up and threw me for a loop once more. This series is definitely keeping me on my toes and I'm having a hard time not wanting to read them all in one go. <br /><br />I can't wait to see what Harrison has up her sleeve next. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15366492278629016250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18640600?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eliel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eliel" href="/user/show/976342-eliel">Eliel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18640600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1189276338066408164">As I said <a href='http://www.carlton-ave.net/books/2006/11/i-used-to-be-fan-of-anita-blake-vampire.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> Kim Harrison's Rachel Morgan series has replaced Laurell Hamilton's Anita Blake series in my mind as top form in the genre of paranormal private investigators.<br/><br/>In this latest outing, she's upped the ante even more by not doing what Hamilton does as her series continues--to wit, regress her plots to the point where they are mere frames on which she hangs her torpidly overwritten soft-core pornography--but instead takes her character the other way. This 6th book of the series takes u</span>
  <span id="freeText1189276338066408164" style="display:none">As I said <a href="http://www.carlton-ave.net/books/2006/11/i-used-to-be-fan-of-anita-blake-vampire.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> Kim Harrison's Rachel Morgan series has replaced Laurell Hamilton's Anita Blake series in my mind as top form in the genre of paranormal private investigators.<br /><br />In this latest outing, she's upped the ante even more by not doing what Hamilton does as her series continues--to wit, regress her plots to the point where they are mere frames on which she hangs her torpidly overwritten soft-core pornography--but instead takes her character the other way. This 6th book of the series takes us along with Rachel as she discovers that there are consequences to living her life as she has been. That her actions have (and can) cause people to lose their lives.<br /><br />It's a breath of fresh air for a writer in this genre to show her readers that she can risk dealing more seriously with her audience. Ms. Harrison has decided that she can risk treating us to Rachel's maturing and in doing so treat us maturely.<br /><br />Thank you, Kim Harrison.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer10543551" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5524782623866572414">wow, i'd forgotten how much kim harrison could totally blow my brains out with her writing. i had been expecting anything but this, and i was actually beginning to think that trent and rachel might actually have a chance together when ceri confirmed who the baby belongs to. plus, i have a feeling minias will survive and become a love interest. there's been too much built up about him for him to just disappear like that, and maybe minias will seek rachel's protection now that newt is openly gunni</span>
  <span id="freeText5524782623866572414" style="display:none">wow, i'd forgotten how much kim harrison could totally blow my brains out with her writing. i had been expecting anything but this, and i was actually beginning to think that trent and rachel might actually have a chance together when ceri confirmed who the baby belongs to. plus, i have a feeling minias will survive and become a love interest. there's been too much built up about him for him to just disappear like that, and maybe minias will seek rachel's protection now that newt is openly gunning.<br /><br />i also have a niggling suspicion about who killed kisten, but i can't be sure yet on that either. my suspect DID say that he would do anything to come closer to ivy and rachel.. i still feel uncomfortable about the sexual tension (or is that what it is?) between rachel and ivy, and i hope rachel finds someone soon. not that she needs to be defined by a male protagonist, but i think it will solve some of her problems (among new ones, i'm sure). and she did say she wanted to have children.. but i was fully satisfied with the ending being what it is, because it may just be the only way to save both ivy and jenks. and in bargaining for information she can also learn about the kisten issue. there's so much to come that i absolutely can't wait for the next book. so many turns i didn't expect in here, and i'm glad she got rid of marshal. dude was really pissing me off. i'm still crossing my fingers on a chance of rachel x trent or rachel x minias though. trent because he simply seems so lonely all the time, and it's obvious he admires her (though by the end of this i don't know if that still applies). minias because he seems to conveniently come to her aid one too many times. he does show his demonic side in this book, but i think it's out of a vested interest in survival rather than outwardly wanting to harm.<br /><br />anyway, i can still see minias coming to rachel as an alternative to newt. but then this would turn into a whole LKH episode, huh? i guess not overly much, then, but kim harrison has such a way of making everything believable. i think she might even manage the love entourage crap if she put her hand to it. the woman weaves magic. i have no doubt that the next book is gonna be even better.</span>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=private-investigator-security">private-investigator-security</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=post-apocalypse">post-apocalypse</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=magic-and-witchcraft">magic-and-witchcraft</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1768298129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16000674548463717387"><b>Where Demons Dare (The Outlaw Demons Wails)</b><br/>4 Stars<br/><br/>As many know from reading my reviews of the series, <i>The Hollows</i> has been more of a miss than a hit. However, this book is a definite move in the right direction.<br/><br/>The ongoing angst between Ivy and Rachel has always been the most significant problem with the books and might have been a deal breaker if GR friends hadn't told me that it is resolved sooner rather than later. Well, that moment arrives here, and Rachel finally makes the mature and sensib</span>
  <span id="freeText16000674548463717387" style="display:none"><b>Where Demons Dare (The Outlaw Demons Wails)</b><br />4 Stars<br /><br />As many know from reading my reviews of the series, <i>The Hollows</i> has been more of a miss than a hit. However, this book is a definite move in the right direction.<br /><br />The ongoing angst between Ivy and Rachel has always been the most significant problem with the books and might have been a deal breaker if GR friends hadn't told me that it is resolved sooner rather than later. Well, that moment arrives here, and Rachel finally makes the mature and sensible decision that she should have made at the outset. It looks like she is growing up at long last. <br /><br />In terms of the plot, someone is helping Rachel's demon nemesis, Algaliarept, escape from his imprisonment in the Ever After, and he has his heart set on throttling her. Trent is forced to swallow is pride and ask Rachel for help in obtaining a crucial ingredient for the cure to the elves genetic issues, and Rachel learns a troubling secret about her parents. All of these seemingly unrelated threads ultimately coalesce into a unified storyline with some exciting actions scenes and an intriguing revelation or two. <br /><br />On a final note, for some unknown reason, the narrator for this installment is Gigi Bermingham instead of Marguerite Gavin. While there is nothing drastically wrong with the narration (other than the occasional discordant pronunciation), she does not have Gavin's range of voices and Jenks, in particular, is not as well done. For me, Gavin is the voice of this series, but I would be willing to listen to other books read by Bermingham. <br /><br />All in all, Harrison has certainly hit her stride with this book. The ongoing character development, the quirky humor and the captivating world building are all finally coming together, and I'm glad that I've stuck with it despite the ups and downs. <br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_11092289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11092289" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63444-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187495654p2/63444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11092289?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/63444-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63444-seth?shelf=modernfantasy">modernfantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63444-seth?shelf=sf-f-h">sf-f-h</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11092289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16731845834944352067">If you've read the first 5 books in the series, you know what to expect. If you haven't, <i>don't start here</i>.<br/><br/>This volume picks up right after book 5, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30259.For_a_Few_Demons_More__The_Hollows___5_' title='For a Few Demons More (The Hollows, #5) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'> For a Few Demons More</a>, which includes some shockers that I really don't want to mention here for anyone who hasn't read that one and it makes talking about ODW difficult without spoiling FFDM.<br/><br/>ODW is similarly dense in twists, turns, and revelations. The official Hollows mailing list banned all discussion of it until six weeks after publication, an un</span>
  <span id="freeText16731845834944352067" style="display:none">If you've read the first 5 books in the series, you know what to expect. If you haven't, <i>don't start here</i>.<br /><br />This volume picks up right after book 5, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30259.For_a_Few_Demons_More__The_Hollows___5_" title="For a Few Demons More (The Hollows, #5) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener"> For a Few Demons More</a>, which includes some shockers that I really don't want to mention here for anyone who hasn't read that one and it makes talking about ODW difficult without spoiling FFDM.<br /><br />ODW is similarly dense in twists, turns, and revelations. The official Hollows mailing list banned all discussion of it until six weeks after publication, an unprecedented move for the list. They opened the list for readers of advanced copies to everyone and moved any discussion of plot--or even reactions to the book as a whole--to there.<br /><br />So, with that caveat, I'll do my best to do this spoiler-free. I will mention things from the first chapter, which has been available in the paperback of FFDM and on Harrison's web site for several months, and anything from books 1-4 is fair game. I'll try to avoid major spoilers for book 5.<br /><br /><br />ODW picks up where FFDM left off. Our protagonists are Rachel Morgan, witch and "runner" (PI-cum-"fixer") and her partners/roommates, Ivy (a vampire in love with Rachel and dealing with shakeups in the criminal underworld she's connected to and could choose to run if she pressed it) and Jenks (a roguish pixy who plays mediator and brings common sense to the team) and their assorted allies, friends, and regulars: the werewolf who has Rachel serve as on-paper Alpha Female of his pack, the elves-in-hiding Trent Kalamack (ally and enemy by turns), Ceri, and Quen, the mysterious witch across the street, and a by-the-book FIB (not a typo--FIB is not FBI) agent. Plus the three demons who have been harassing Rachel for books on end, now seemingly no longer restricted by the contracts that bound them and fighting desperately for their own lives, using Rachel as a bargaining chip.<br /><br />Oh, and her mom. Her mom's a major character in this one.<br /><br />And right there we see the major point of ODW. The series has always had a huge focus on family, both chosen and born. Rachel forms a family with her business partner and with a small werewolf pack, and recovers her ties to her blood family while driving herself to live up to her father's legacy. Ivy deals with the psychological damage the criminal and corrupt vampire community (run, like the agency that polices vampires, by her extended family) has done. Jenks fights from day one to protect his family against the day he dies, which is coming far too soon. And the elves are trying to rescue their whole species, which is so much in danger of dying that they've faked their own genocide to maintain their culture.<br /><br />So Rachel winds up having to work with her mother and reveal some of the dangers she faces in her daily life. In exchange, her mother reveals... well... quite a few things. Her mother is mostly doing well in this book; she has few of the lapses into confusion and dementia that have plagued her since her husband died and Rachel works to understand what her mother needs in her life, as well as leaning what her mother can do to help them both.<br /><br />Harrison is at her best when she focuses on the relationships between the characters(*) and how Rachel and Ivy are learning to connect with other people; this book has a lot of navel-gazing, but it's interesting navel-gazing and never gets in the way of the story. <br /><br />This is a book of revelations: secrets about Rachel's mother (and father) that go as deep as the ones revealed in books 1 and 2, secrets about the elves (although revelations about them are a staple of 5 of the 6 books), and even secrets about the demons. Harrison is revealing some of the history, convolutions, and even magical theory behind the Hollows. She's at her best when writing complex, interconnected storylines and pulling back the covers inch-by-teasing-inch(*).<br /><br /><br />As the title suggests, the major action revolves around the demons. The "outlaw demon" is Big Al (her not-so-affectionate nickname for the demon who vexes her life the most), who was imprisoned in the last book for breaking laws and endangering all the demons' livelihood. Someone is summoning him out of the demons' custody and setting him free to do what he wants, which is to kill or kidnap Rachel. Rachel has to navigate demon politics (and legal system!), keep Al off her back, find the person summoning him and find out why s/he's doing it, and try to keep the deadly and enigmatic demon Newt from getting involved. And if she can learn something about why she is one of two witches in the world who can perform demonic magic along the way, all the better.<br /><br />On top of this, of course, Trent has "urgent" (and risky) business he'll cajole, threaten, or trick Rachel into doing for him. As usual.<br /><br />And, of course, deal with her family as her mom gets more involved than Rachel ever wanted.<br /><br />The book has the usual good action scenes--Harrison is at her best with the action(*)--with the chases, skulking, bluffing, magical attacks, and shoot-outs we've come to expect Rachel to get herself into. Every one makes sense and none get too long or convoluted. Harrison's writing on this has improved steadily across the series.<br /><br />We have the expected evolution of Rachel and Ivy's ongoing and messy relationship. It isn't as mesmerizing or intense as in the last two books and doesn't have the pyrotechnic writing of books one and five, but it works great and leads to a truly beautiful and heart-wrenching moment. As we saw in FFDM, Ivy is maturing emotionally at an amazing rate and we get a touching insight into her life, especially after the events in FFDM that turned her emotional life upside-down.<br /><br /><br />So, net net. Is it a good book? Yes. Is it the best book in the series? Hard to say. It has the most information and advances the world story the furthest, but it's not the most "detectivey," "noir," or funny (although I wanted to read funny lines to my girlfriend all throughout, as usual; she forbade me to since they <i>all</i> had spoilers). If you're doing to read book 7, you have to read this one, of course, and you will enjoy doing so. It just may well have some of your favorite moments.<br /><br /><br />* And I should clear one thing up. Kim Harrison is at her best when she's writing. At least, she is as a writer; I don't know about her personal life. The writing in this series started good, with moments of pyrotechnic genius, and it's just getting better as the characters and world settle in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16731845834944352067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1579827739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579827739" />
    <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire"><img alt="Beth The Vampire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483516030p2/22241496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1579827739?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth The Vampire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth The Vampire" href="/user/show/22241496-beth-the-vampire">Beth The Vampire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/2334647.Where_Demons_Dare">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=series-6-to-10">series-6-to-10</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=witches-wizards">witches-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22241496-beth-the-vampire?shelf=demons">demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579827739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14664701393553557987"><b>Happily into the ever-after.</b><br/><br/>Oh my dear, sweet Rachel. Finally recognising her dangerous, risk taking ways and you end up right back where you started. But this time, instead of cursing at you loudly from my bed at midnight, I was right behind you.<br/><br/>The fallout from the previous book was massive, with white witch Rachel and her vampire roommate and business partner, Ivy, having to come to terms with their overwhelming grief. While always in the back of their minds, this part of the story didn't see</span>
  <span id="freeText14664701393553557987" style="display:none"><b>Happily into the ever-after.</b><br /><br />Oh my dear, sweet Rachel. Finally recognising her dangerous, risk taking ways and you end up right back where you started. But this time, instead of cursing at you loudly from my bed at midnight, I was right behind you.<br /><br />The fallout from the previous book was massive, with white witch Rachel and her vampire roommate and business partner, Ivy, having to come to terms with their overwhelming grief. While always in the back of their minds, this part of the story didn't seem to dominate, and I'm assuming that there is more to come.<br /><br />I won't even try to summarise the plot or anything, because there are so many threads, but also I don't want to spoil anything for those who have not read the previous books (which is a must!). But I will say that this addition to the series is more focused around demons and the ever-after than the vampires which dominated the last book. There are so many beings trying to kill Rachel, we just have to take them one at a time.<br /><br />It seemed like there were so many revelations in <i>Where Demons Dare</i>, and I imagine that Rachel was felt quite emotionally overwhelmed. The truth about her father, where witches came from, her being able to spindle demon magic, Ceri's pregnancy, and the threat she poses to the whole of the world. Rachel keeps on taking hit after hit, which I guess is why I was with her all the way at the end. Usually I would be screaming at her to make a proper plan, think about what she's going to do for one friggin' second, CALM THE HELL DOWN! But not this time. I wanted her to show everyone that she had this under control; that she was smart, strong, and not what everyone else thought of her. It was a powerful moment, and one that redeemed a lot about Rachel for me.<br /><br /><b>So I dealt in demons. So the <i>hell</i> what. It didn't make me a bad person. Or stupid. Or rash. It made me dangerous to everyone around me is all.</b><br /><br />What I love about this series is the characters, which is becoming quite a cast of different people. There is Jenks, the pixy and Rachel's other business partner, Trent, Ceri and Quinn, the elves, Glen, the FIB officer, David, Rachel's pack-mate and resident alpha werewolf, Marshall, another witch and potential love interest, Kelsey, Rachel's neighbour who she just found out the true identity of, Rachel's mom (who is hilarious), Takata, the famous rock star with a secret link to Rachel, and then there are demons galore with Al, Minias, and Newt. But it is never confusing, never tedious. All of these people are important to Rachel (except the demons....she spends most of the book trying to get them away from her), and despite all these people, in a way she is still alone. She is one of a kind, in body and spirit, always with a mountain to climb, with a hell of a journey in front of her.<br /><br />Making deals with demons is never going to be easy, and just when Rachel thinks she may have the upper hand, she is pulled right back into the middle. But I think now that she is beginning to come to terms with what she is and what she can do, she will be all the stronger for it. I really enjoyed this addition to the series, and it is definitely one of the best so far.<br /><br /><b>"You can't forget anything," I said, watching the words vanish into nothing. "And even if you do, it always comes back to bitch-slap you in the morning."</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14664701393553557987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_147259405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147259405" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147259405?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=hollows">hollows</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147259405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer347784146240445869">I still haven't recovered from what happened to Kisten... and even though three months have passed for Rachel since the events of the last book, she hasn't either. But she is trying. Of course, even when she is trying to piece her life together, more circumstances beyond her control arise to make it all fall apart again. In this case, it's Al. He's back and he is royally ticked off. The demon blames Rachel for the fact that he is in trouble in the ever-after and he plans on punishing her every t</span>
  <span id="freeText347784146240445869" style="display:none">I still haven't recovered from what happened to Kisten... and even though three months have passed for Rachel since the events of the last book, she hasn't either. But she is trying. Of course, even when she is trying to piece her life together, more circumstances beyond her control arise to make it all fall apart again. In this case, it's Al. He's back and he is royally ticked off. The demon blames Rachel for the fact that he is in trouble in the ever-after and he plans on punishing her every time someone summons him out. And that has been happening with increasing frequency. <br /><br />In the meantime, Trent is back in her orbit. He wants her help to get a genetic sample from the elves in the ever-after. He believes if he gets an old enough sample, he can use it to genetically alter and save the future of his race... and Ceri's unborn child. <br /><br />This book is a lot more action oriented than most Hollows books. Usually, the character development puts the happenings of the story firmly in the backseat. That's not so here. Sure, we have some residual heartache over Kisten, some angst about Rachel's family history, and the ever-present will-they-or-won't-they with Ivy. But I was actually more wrapped up with the momentum of the action this time --and frankly, I was glad for it. After the emotional wringer Kim Harrison put me through last time, it was nice not to read the book through tears. <br /><br />We take a fantastic trip to the much-anticipated ever-after. We meet more demons and get an unexpected look inside their world. Plus a pretty big reveal as to why Rachel is so special and what that means for demon-kind. <br /><br />A great book that really moved the overall story forward and opens the doors for many new possibilities in the next installment. 5 stars <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="347784146240445869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7043761174790975565">4.5 stars<br/><br/>The first half was really slow and I was questioning why I had given it such a high rating when I first read it. The second half was so good. I'm finally beginning to see why it was I loved this series so much.<br/><br/>Rachel finally showed significant growth. She still has a tendency to mouth off like an idiotic teenager, but she's making much better decisions, which is a huge step for her. I was so happy that Rachel figured out what she does and doesn't want from Ivy because I hated the weird </span>
  <span id="freeText7043761174790975565" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />The first half was really slow and I was questioning why I had given it such a high rating when I first read it. The second half was so good. I'm finally beginning to see why it was I loved this series so much.<br /><br />Rachel finally showed significant growth. She still has a tendency to mouth off like an idiotic teenager, but she's making much better decisions, which is a huge step for her. I was so happy that Rachel figured out what she does and doesn't want from Ivy because I hated the weird drama between them. It was impressive that she did right by Quen and Trent despite the issues she has with them.<br /><br />The revelations about Rachel were surprising. She knew she was more than a witch but had no idea how much more. The stuff that was revealed about her family wasn't all that interesting. It's not like any of that needed to be part of the story to explain what she is. <br /><br />The parts with Trent were my favorite. He hasn't changed but the more page time he gets the more is learned about him. He's nowhere near as cruel and heartless as Rachel initially thought he was. There wasn't a cliffhanger at the end but I'm looking forward to the next one.</span>

<div id="review_896440511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/896440511" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16417346-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528189144p2/16417346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/896440511?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/16417346-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=magic-summoning-witches-wizards">magic-summoning-witches-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16417346-marianne?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer896440511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10065228725939615352">Re-read October 2020<br/><br/>I'm still reeling from the shocking, shocking end of For a Few Demons More, and it made me wonder if the series could bounce back. And yes; it did. In fact, the second half of this book, with amazing action and twists was superb. However, something in this book just rubbed me the wrong way. Rachel is, understandably, still dealing with loss and grief. But you know what: Each time Rachel tries to cope with the pain, it feels like Kim Harrison is just rubbing it in my face: "Ha</span>
  <span id="freeText10065228725939615352" style="display:none">Re-read October 2020<br /><br />I'm still reeling from the shocking, shocking end of For a Few Demons More, and it made me wonder if the series could bounce back. And yes; it did. In fact, the second half of this book, with amazing action and twists was superb. However, something in this book just rubbed me the wrong way. Rachel is, understandably, still dealing with loss and grief. But you know what: Each time Rachel tries to cope with the pain, it feels like Kim Harrison is just rubbing it in my face: "Haha, I'm the author and if I want to kill your favorite character, I will, so just deal with it!" <br />Is it immature of me to detract a star from my rating? Probably, but when an author kills my favorite character, and then proceeds to rub salt in an open wound, there must be consequences. *Sigh*<br /><br />Luckily, we get plenty of Al in this installment. I have enjoyed the demon interaction since Al first made an appearance, and even when he has been at his worst, I have still liked his character. There is especially a potent kitchen scene where the changes start shifting, and the end and how it all turns out almost made me do a literal high five. Their conversation in the park turned out to be one of my favorite scenes ever in the Hollows series. Toss in Newt, Minias, and additional demon law and exploration of the Ever-After, and this book climbed even further up my happy-read-o-meter. (And Newt: I hope you catch Minias, he deserves it;-) BTW: Al’s subsequent bet was hilarious.)<br /><br />Charismatic new vampire Master Ryn Cormel's entrance was also one of my favorite scenes of the series. I'm referring to Ivy once again obliviously embarrassing Rachel to death with the mention of the "vamp guide" in front of him. (He's the author.) It would be neat if there could be a companion guide to the series published, "The Vampire Dating Guide." Of course this could never happen since so much of it is clearly... *cough*... preeeeeetty graphic… <br /><br />What I truly liked in this novel were the surprises: Learning what Trent was holding from Rachel, not just her mom’s shocking family secret, but what his father's altering her DNA had actually done. The search for a vampire killer is on, Rachel is asked to go on a mission into the Ever-After to retrieve a sample of elvin DNA by none other than Trent (still an absolute ASS), Minias wants Rachel to exchange summoning names with Al, so that he can't be summoned out from the Ever-After, jailed or not. (Wow, that particular event really set the wheels in motion.) Additionally, Ceri’s been keeping secrets from Rachel too. Quite a few tense and angry scenes in this book. As for Bis the gargoyle; he seems to have popped in from out of nowhere. What’s he doing there, what role will he play in events to come? The dialogue between Jenks and Bis had me giggling quite a few times.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed the last half of The Outlaw Demon Wails. The ending rocks and the change isn't something I could have anticipated, but I loved it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10065228725939615352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20176997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20176997" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112377-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217926616p2/112377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20176997?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/112377-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of urban fantasy and those who've enjoyed the series so far!</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20176997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6314077452422980405">This is the sixth book in the Rachel Morgan series. The demon Algaliarept is supposed to be imprisoned in the Ever-After, but someone has been summoning him nightly, putting Rachel and the ones she loves at risk. Rachel joins forces with Glenn from the FIB to find out who, while Ivy investigates a mystery left over from book 5. This was a terrific read, although in some ways less satisfying to me than the earlier books. I wanted answers, and you do get a lot here---everything but the answer I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText6314077452422980405" style="display:none">This is the sixth book in the Rachel Morgan series. The demon Algaliarept is supposed to be imprisoned in the Ever-After, but someone has been summoning him nightly, putting Rachel and the ones she loves at risk. Rachel joins forces with Glenn from the FIB to find out who, while Ivy investigates a mystery left over from book 5. This was a terrific read, although in some ways less satisfying to me than the earlier books. I wanted answers, and you do get a lot here---everything but the answer I wanted most! That missing answer is also connected to a plot thread I felt was kind of dropped, as though the author lost interest. Having said that, let me say that there were also a lot of things this book did better than earlier entries in the series. It's nice to have some interaction between Rachel and her actual family, in addition to the family of friends she has created. Rachel also becomes aware of how many people really care about her, which is especially nice in a series that has been full of uneasy alliances (I imagine, though, her relations with Trent Kalamack are always going to flip flop around). Rachel is growing up, and trying to leave her thrill-seeking behind her; her new method of reaching decisions is to believe if it feels right, it must be wrong. All in all, <i>The Outlaw Demon Wails</i> is an entertaining paranormal read which ties up some loose ends, but leaves enough hanging that I want to read the next book right now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6314077452422980405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45600494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45600494" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1605591-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252166169p2/1605591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45600494?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/1605591-christine">Christine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061149825" href="/book/show/2800881-the-outlaw-demon-wails">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=witches-and-wizards">witches-and-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=minority-and-women-writers">minority-and-women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=weres-and-shifters">weres-and-shifters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer45600494&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45600494" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13023544686950676839"><i>The Outlaw Demon Wails</i> seems to be a bridge book in <i>The Hollows</i> series, and maybe that is why I thought this book was the weakest in the series. There are some resolutions to questions that have been building in the books, such as the Ivy/Rachel relationship and how exactly Rachel can do some of the things she does. Sadly, the book itself feels too long and has too many plot points that are superfluous or dropped. For instance, Rachel discovers that her father is not, in fact, her biological fat</span>
  <span id="freeText13023544686950676839" style="display:none"><i>The Outlaw Demon Wails</i> seems to be a bridge book in <i>The Hollows</i> series, and maybe that is why I thought this book was the weakest in the series. There are some resolutions to questions that have been building in the books, such as the Ivy/Rachel relationship and how exactly Rachel can do some of the things she does. Sadly, the book itself feels too long and has too many plot points that are superfluous or dropped. For instance, Rachel discovers that her father is not, in fact, her biological father. The point does not seem to add much to the series, except give Rachel more angst and a still alive father, perhaps making her more special in a sense because of it. While I understand that recaps are needed for new readers. The recaps in this book were too long and filled too much space. Additionally some characters, like Ivy, felt flat, and the term “hip cocked” was used too much. Way too much. <br />	Happily, all the things that make the series good are still present, such as the humor and the fact that Rachel’s powers have costs. Unlike some other series, power in <i>The Hollows</i> has a price, and even while Rachel becomes a little more powerful (perhaps simply more aware of her power) that too has a price, a heavy price. It is nice to see that in a book. Rachel herself also grows up and grows more aware. It was nice to see her mother have a larger role as well. Additionally, the paperback edition has a nice short story about Ceri. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13023544686950676839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393387303" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11667609-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483756840p2/11667609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/11667609-lauren">Lauren</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393387303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10926050654866358785">I didn't know how I was going to make it through this book knowing that Kisten wouldn't be waiting for me on the pages. I tried to console myself - I told myself that with Kisten gone, it clears the path for Rachel & Trent to possibly get together.... But then I remember how much I loved Kisten & how much I'm going to miss him... <br/><a href='http://s1272.photobucket.com/user/elle_rachelle/media/online%20uploads/457822_zps3dd99af0.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388683662ra/7901663.gif' alt=' photo 457822_zps3dd99af0.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>
  <i>Ok, it's time to move on...</i>
</b><br/>Three months have passed for Rachel since the<br/>events of the last book & like me - she's having a little trouble moving forward with he</span>
  <span id="freeText10926050654866358785" style="display:none">I didn't know how I was going to make it through this book knowing that Kisten wouldn't be waiting for me on the pages. I tried to console myself - I told myself that with Kisten gone, it clears the path for Rachel &amp; Trent to possibly get together.... But then I remember how much I loved Kisten &amp; how much I'm going to miss him... <br><a href="http://s1272.photobucket.com/user/elle_rachelle/media/online%20uploads/457822_zps3dd99af0.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388683662ra/7901663.gif" alt=" photo 457822_zps3dd99af0.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <i>Ok, it's time to move on...</i>
</b><br>Three months have passed for Rachel since the<br>events of the last book &amp; like me - she's having a little trouble moving forward with her life. She is trying, of course - but I don't blame her... I mean - how can you??? &amp; naturally more circumstances completely beyond her control arise that push her to fall apart all over again. <i>Poor girl just can't catch a break...</i><br><br>Al is back and he is royally pissed off!<br><a href="http://s1272.photobucket.com/user/elle_rachelle/media/online%20uploads/700244_zpscfqkxafu.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388683662ra/7901664.gif" alt=" photo 700244_zpscfqkxafu.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>He apparently blames Rachel for his in trouble in the ever-after and he plans on making her pay - big time! <br><br>One of the things I've always liked about the Hollows is that there is never a shortage of new characters. In this book we are treated to several new characters, all more interesting then the next. <br><br>Bis was a nice surprise and look forward to more of him. I think it's neat that Rachel has her own gargoyle now. I can't wait to see what kind of adventures this opens doors to!<br><br>&amp; now with Piscary out of the picture, we have the chance to learn more about the new master vampire, Rynn Cormel. As of now I don't think he's downright evil.... not like Piscary was, but this guy is definitely no push-over, that's for damn sure!<br><br>Also, it was fun seeing more of Rachel's mom. After meeting her, it definitely goes a long way toward explaining why Rachel is the hot mess that she is. I loved her - so funny! <br><br>I'm more then ready for Marshall to exit stage left. His whole white knight fetish is getting real old, real quick! Rachel is more than capable of taking care of herself - the last thing she needs is some hairless wonder playing at being her knight in shinning armor! <br><br>&amp; with that being said, Rachel really has grown up over these last few books. She's still a mess but now she's thinking before she acts. She's clearly starting a new phase in her life....<br><br>The events with Trent and the ever-after were interesting, I love him &amp; Rachel together. &amp; when they were roller skating together - <b>*cue the girly sigh*</b> <i>because there definitely was one!</i> <br><br>Another awesome addition to Rachel Morgan's ongoing emotional rollercoaster &amp; life of adventure! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10926050654866358785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
